Sept 58

27 Jan 68 to
17 July 72

PCS, Buenos Aires, Argentina as Second Secy, then
promoted to First Secy, Soviet Embassy, Cultural
Section.
May 1975

(Latin America Dept)
Replacement Pattern:
Mexico: ALPERYEV replaced Vasily Mikhaylovich CHICHKOV (201-0207254)
and was replaced by Vladimir Agafonovich DOLGOV (201-0762036)
both known KGB officers.
Argentina: ALFERYEV replaced Viktor Mikhaylovich FILIPPOV (MD 001706)
and was reported as a subpoct KGB Resident in Be As.
ALFERYEV was replaced by Sajlily Mikhaylovich MURAVVEY (201-3586530)
WHOM Hg. Employees was KGB Resident (Suspect) during his tour
in Bs.As.
Peru:
ALFERYEV to replace Arseniy Fedorovich ORLOV (201- 0727613)
as Counselor of Embassy, Lima Poru. ORLOV was carried as
Suspect KCB Resident in Lima, ALFERYEV will be carried in
same capacity as Suspect KGB Resident.
ALFERYEV arrived Lima PCS early March 1976 or late Feb 1976.

se hablande con su marrido de una combinación financiero que
fracase. Utiliande au pesición de diplesation hace contra-
hande-hermias de perfumas repa y pielos a URH3. Utilisa
servicios de oficiales de de fient pascuera e comercial
sevietica que la Vietan experimentente.

SPECIAL REF-RT
6F
1.- SURJECT
Ivan Gavrilovich ALPERIEV was born in Moscow (U.S.S.R.), on the
20th of January 1928, diplomatic passport No. 091.477, married to Rosa
Alekreevna ALFERIEVA, born on September 20th, 1934, in Moscow, diplomatic
passport No. 019.468. Subject is assigned as 2nd Counsellor of the U.S.S.R.
Embassy in Buenos Aires. He arrived in this country on the 27th of January
1968, taking up residence on Uruguay 1176, Sth Floor, Apt. "A" in the Federal
Capital, Tel. 41-5405, living at said address until de 7th of October 1969
when he moved to live at the Posadas Club (residence for the officers of the
soviet representation).
ALFERIEV had been for a short t'me in Argentina during the month
of September 1958; in Havana in September 194.11 in Quito in January and February
1963 and in Tijuana in September 1963. He was representative of PRAVDA in
Mexico during 1960 and 1964.
In view of the fact that subject lived separately from the rest
of the Embassy personnel, his mission based on information was thus made easier.
It should be pointed out, that during his residence on Uruguay,
he was kept under surveillance through a technical penetration carried out
by this Section.
As a result of the exploitation of these lines, as well as the
Case "ASADO" (summer home) and information from the "LORO" case, certain details
concerning his personality, private life and contacts have been ascertained.
Throug+ thorough study of above mentioned sources, it is apparent
that the ALFERIEVS have certain differences, during which he is the object
of vituperation from his wife Ross, which Ivan thoroughly ignores to the
great exasperation of his wife.
11.- PERSONALITY OF IVAN ALFERIEV
No is an introvert, clever, cautious and distrustful. He knows
how to hide his feelings and he has an excellent self-centrol, showing violent
feelings on very rare occasions. (See Section IV).
With relaticn to his cultural level, nothing much is known, as
he has never been heard speaking on themen of general culture. When he speaks
at social gatherings he is joking, using double meaning phrases (usually funny)
Sle att 1 to HABA 01080 CS COPY
201-236701


- 2 -
or he tells jokes. It is as though he were afraid to show that he takes
things seriously, as though he were ashamed or frightened.
During the various opportunities when his wife is screaming all
sort of improprieties at him he maintains absolute silence, seeming to be
concentrating on one fixed idea, and letting all that Rosa says just slide
eff him.
He has been identified and known to belong to the K.O.B. (Soviet
Secret Police). According to a confidential source, he is considered a high
official in the embassy and of absoluto trustworthiness by Ambassador Iouro
VOLSKI! being respected and feared by the rest of the embassy staff. He
speaks perfect spanish.
He is present at all receptions with Iouri VOLSKI and Ivan DIAKOV
(ambassador and Chief of the Commercial Representation, respectively), not
only in his official position, but also in his private life, having a warm
friendship between the three which is quite rare in the embassy circle. During
his stay at the summer home, ALFRIKIV and his wife occupy the quasters reserved
for the ambassador.
III.- PERSONALITY OF ROSA ALYPRIEVA
A certain duality of personality is apparent in her behavior. In
her married life she shows herself to be intolerant andimpetuous, arriving
at absoluteilack of control on various occasions, bringing forth continual
maitel quarrels.
On the contrary, in her social life, she shows herself as a very
decile, cheerful woman, being the center of attraction in almost all the
gatheringe for her "lovely disposition" and gayety, not only among the men
but also their wives. (See section I).
Ross Alekscevs ALFERIRVA is a woman brought up in the typical
soviet atmosphere, subjected sice childhood to a rigid political indoctrination
us some juvenile organization and in school. She is not sufficiently intelligent
to rid herself, even partially, of what she has been taught. She does not sepa-
rate her affective life from the obligations that she, presumes, every
citisens should have. it seems that the does not realize the importance of
her husbands miseion. She is not a woman who is attuned to her companion.
She is not on the same wave length, she does not understand him. She harbors
a
concentrated and continuous resentment against him. May, be this is due to
his imnicand keen and wounding sense of humour.


14/20/00
- 3 -
With regard to her surroundings, this woman has shown, on various
opportunities, to feel antizesty and scorr for Argentina and its people, ducugh
probably to its leanings toward democracy, and therefore, contrary to her way
of thinking. As she has shown not to possess much imagination, she takes as
wonderful that which she has been taught. However, the reason for her poor
matrimonial relations remains a mystery. Maybe one of the reason, as stated
above is her lack of understanding of her husband, so that one quarrel on top
of the other has built a wall which cannot be breached.
In the company of her friends, Rosa has always shown herself to
be pleasant, gay and uncomplicated. She has not always masked her marital
problems, so that they are work a secret to the rest of the members of the
embassy, who nevertheless make believe they know nothing about it, through
consideration or whatever other motives they may have. On some occasions
VOLSKI has taken the initiative to improve relations between the ALFERIEVS,
to no avail.
IV.- MODUS OTERANDI WHICH WAS SHOWN UP FROM SURVEILLANCE
During the shadowing of Ivan ALFERIIV, he has shown himself to
be an expert in this matter. We is observant and his movements in the street
are carried out carefully and ablyy- on many opportunities he has shaken off
his shadows. He is an excellent driver, and he uses all sorts of ruses to
show off the agents on the job. This is proved below:
Shadowing on 23-5-691
No drove his car down Cordena Av., turned on $ July going towards Cerrite,
which was closed off for repairs. In the middle of the street were two
signs which read: "DETOUR, WSK CENTER LANES". Subject disregarded the signs
and continued straizht ahead towards Viamonte, where transit was completely
sut off, and he had to take $ July again and comes to the obelisco.
With this trick, ALFERIEV wanted to learn whether he was being
followed.
SHADOWING on 20-5-69:
He vent into the Bank of Napol, approaches the counter, carries on a conversation
with an employee, and vanishes without being observed aspite of close vigilance
Before going into a building of store, he looks in buch directions and searches
surefully.
When he goes in his car, he drives slowly, but every so often, he steps on
the gas, and then abruptly reduces speed, doing this various times.


- 4 -
--buring all the shadowings carried put, subject always managed to go ahead
on the yellow light, leaving his shadows generally. facing the red light.
- On various occasions he wast up one way streets,
V.- CONTACTS
It was ascertained that ALFENKIV arrived home very late at night
and even at dawn, which is quite out of the o-dilwery with the rest of the
diplomatic personnel. (See Annex 2).
This led to the supposition that subject was either leading a
licentious life or carrying out clandestine activities. Therefore, a permanent
surveveillance was carried out during 24 hours for 20 days on his home, proving
that he d'ed in reality come home between 6 and 7 at times.
Fifteen days before his return to the U.S.S.R. for his leave,
a surveillance and shadowing service was set up during all 24 hours, proving
that subject did make clandestine contacts.
It was under these circumstances that on the 21/5/69, at 1200 hours,
a contact was spotted. This occurred once again on the 33/5/69, at which time
the "contact" was suspicious of being followed and he pulled quickly out of the
area.
On the 16th of August of the present year, when a security agent who
was carrying out his duties on the ALFERIY address (improvement of the P.T.),
spotted the above mentioned contact patrolling the ince; with the aid of a Polic-
man he was detained in order to be identified, his documents are the following:

VI. CONCLUSIONS
With reference to the 2nd Councillor of the U.S.A.R., Ivan ALFERIEV,
the following conclusions have been reached:
a) He is a diplomatic officer who carries out his professional vort efficiently,
showing at all times great sagacity when carrying out public contacts and
relations, avoiding on various opportunities with ingenuity and ability the
shadowing detail assined to him.
b) With reference to his relations and activities within theMabassay, it is
observed that he carries a lot of veight over the rest of the personnel, as
he is given deferential attention and respect not only at official but
private functions within the circle.
o) He is a person who is always busy, on the go all day and on into the late
hours of the night.
d) His married life is not harmonious, due to the charecter of his wife who is
temperamental and impetuous and not tolerant toward subject. It is estimated
that these misunderstandings are linked to his activities outside of normal
working hours, which take him away from home, as vell as, the indifference
and silence with which her recriminations are received.
o) With reference to his contacts, mentioned in this report, the corresponding
investigations are being carried out to determine how for they reach and their
importance.

References: A. BUENOS AIRES-3801, 2 October 1969
B. BUENOS AIRES-3837, 9 October 1969
1. We have kept you up to date on AECOR'S sudden move and the
subsequent termination of AELANYARD. At the present time, we still
do not know whether or not the story of a sudden transfer to Mexico
City was in reality the basis for the move or if a compromise of the
operation was the actual cause. As we pointed out in our criginal
cable, our immediate thought was that perhaps the AECORMAN slip
had caused all AEXICE types to "pull in" and that perhaps AECOOF
was simply following orders. Subsequent investigation, however,
tended to be a "sufficient" of the AECOR.
The AELANYARD transcripts reveal that AECOR did indeed
contemplate the move several days before we actually had wind of it.
His wife did not like the idea and complained to him about the
move. AEROOR also told his landlord in advance of his move. There
is also evidence that AECOR was in somewhat regular contact with
the Mexican Embassy and although we were not certain, it appeared
that he was anxious to learn if his visa had been granted. In
any case, on 26 September 1969, AECORO and wife checked out of
their own.
3. Shortly thereafter, we made a physical check of the interior
of the apartment. Everything seemed to be in order. There was no
evidence whatsoever that the technical end of the operation had
been tampered with. As we said boiore, it functioned up until and
after AESORO vacated.
Continued.

4. We have not beow able as yet to establish direct social
contact with ABEOOR. Both Nina T. MARGANDE and Paul W. I.EVERONE
(who have legitimate reason to seek him out) have tried, but to
date, to no avail. Our hope has been to have ABEOOR actually tell
us of his plans - will he indeed be transforved to Mexico? Our
original thought was that the Mexico Station could readily determine
if he has been able to perform for a visa to that country. As you know,
we struck out here also.
5. The fact is that as of this writing, we do not know
whether ABEOOR's move was routine and innocent or if indeed there
was a nouthing sinitton involved. If ABEOOR does indeed pick up
and move to Mexico, we shall, of course, be somewhat relieving
However, this will not answer categorically the major vision -
was the operation compromised? It would appear that regardless of
what happens to ABEOOR, we shall never know to actual reason for
his move. However, for what it is worth, the evidence here does
not point toward a compromise.

KOROFAIA
RYBAT REDTOP ALIANYARD
Transmittal of Tapes
References
A. HABA-20415, dated 27 March 1969
B. LABW-11445, dated 21 April 1969
1. Forwarded under separate cover are two AZLANYARD
tapes covering 28, 27 and 28 July 1969. The recording for
the 28th runs through the last half of the first tape and
all of the second; it involves a conversation between
ABECOM and 201-268170 regarding the lurmer's experiences
during his recent home leave. We should very much
appreciation to the headquarters' monitors review this
basis. The situation is not a major challenge for
complete a transcription as possible. Once the transcription
is finished the tapes may be destroyed.
2. In reference B Headquarters suggested that samplings
of AELANYARD be forwarded tri-annully. Since we have begun
forwarding the most interesting AELANYARD tapes for transcrip-
tion at Headquarters, we assume there is no longer any need
to transmit routine samplings of the initial DIOGENESIS
product.
Mora 7. MARGANDE
Hina T. MARGANDE
Attachments:
8 Tapes U/B/C
